Left this as a reply but I feel it deserves its own comment: Hi there! I make a lot of Cola at home for my family, you don't need ANY food coloring, no offense intended to FlavorLab but this isn't the best way to color it, and actually I'll tell you what I do and what Coca Cola itself does, and you don't need to buy anything extra! Here you go: when you're making the caramel at the beginning, add a little bit of water, like a few drops to a teaspoon, and cook it a bit longer than the video suggests, until it starts to smell very toasted a bit like chocolate chip cookies and turns ALMOST black, very dark red / very dark brown, then make the cola the rest of the way as the video suggests and it will be very dark without a need for added food color; what I'm telling you about is how to make "caramel coloring", you should look a recipe up here on youtube, it's the way store bought colas and root beers, and even some sauces and gravies, are colored! It can add a bitter / sour taste a bit like coffee, that you can reduce by adding more sugar and lime juice. And PS replace the carrier oil you're using with MCT oil, olive oil, vegetable oil, or canola oil, those won't get solid like coconut oil does when they get cold. And if you plan on making this a lot, you can put a whole bunch of the aromatics into a bunch of alcohol and leave it for a few weeks and you can make what's called a "flavor extract" or "tincture" and use that in place of the oil altogether, like was mentioned in the video ü§†

Y'all are making jokes about Coca-Cola having cocaine in it and that that's why he said it doesn't taste quite right, but you're not far off the truth.   While actual cocaine has not been used for many, many, many years, Coca-Cola is the only company in the United States, that I am aware of, that is allowed to used coca leaves in their product.   Now notice I said leaves, not cocaine. When Coca leaves haves their cocaine content extracted for use in various medical and scientific trials, they spent leaves are then sent to Coca-Cola who then use them to flavor the beverage.  So yeah, if you can get some spent coca leaves... should help!

OK what I learned from my attempt: 1. I used ground cinnamon, nutmeg and coriander because un-ground ones were ridiculously expensive since they were only available in the Healthy Food section; it works OK, but use about half the amount of ground cinnamon; 2. If you're using ground ingredients, you must mix the oil during those 30 minutes or they might burn very easily and ruin the whole mixture; also it'll taint the oil dark brownish, but once you strain it it'll return to yellow; 3. 400 g of sugar is still hella sweet, I'll try 250 g next time; 4. For some reason when I poured the water into the caramel, it turned really red, like, literally blood. This is apparently normal; 5. I used lime juice concentrate (two tablespoons = one lime juice) and it did not turn green; but I'm still using a black food coloring next time because it looks too much like diluted energy drink; 6. Coffee filters take forever to strain the oil, I'll try cheese cloth or something along these lines next time.

Coke company actually uses lavender as one of the essential flavouring oils, alongside with orange, coriander and nutmeg. The colour of modern colas comes from a specific cocaine and novocaine tea leaf. They extract the caine molecules with steeping process, siphon off the caine chemicals and sell that off to pharmaceutical companies and then do a second brewing process. This helps to give colas their dark red/brown tea like colour

You seem to have completely missed the point that a real cola drink is flavoured with extract of the cola nut. Where is your flavour component for that?? For sure, you have produced a possibly pleasant fruit & spice flavoured soft drink, but for you to call it "cola" is stretching the bounds of artistic licence too far. I am a qualified Food Technologist and worked as a Product Development Chemist and Quality Control Manager in a soft drinks factory for many years, and I'd like to tell you your list of ingredients at 0m50 is *nowhere close* to the real recipe. Also missing is the "metallic" taste of coke, and this comes from a low dosage of phosphoric acid - not sure is this is available for purchase to ordinary citizens. The citric acid from the lime you used is a good substitute, but just doesn't give the required tang/bite.

We analysed Cola in one of our chemistry lessons and one important ingredient misses in your recipe (and thats why you think that there is too much sugar): the phospor acid. There is so much sugar in Cola that normal you would have to vomit after drinking one sip, but with the acid you dont have to. So you get like the energy boost from the sugar (which is the reason why so many people drink it) but dont really feel the amount of sugar because of the acid.  Fun fact: the ph-value we got for coca cola im class was around 0,4-0,6 which is less than the ph-value of your stomach acid (1-1,5).   And yes our teacher destroyed the taste of cola for us

Really, there are two flavours of cola. Coke and Pepsi are one flavour, and cola sweets/cheap supermarket cola is the second "candy" cola flavour. You will get 90% of the way that candy cola flavour with fresh lime juice and cinnamon. Just those two.. it's a magical combination and is a great base to build your first cola beverage on. Try the ingredients that Flavor Lab uses here too to hone in on your perfect cola taste but know that lime juice and cinnamon are the magic ingredients..

Fun bit of trivia. Coca Cola gets it's name and flavor from the combination of the 7X and Coca extract. (The 7x recipe of the time had the Kola Nut as part of the ingredients. That's not common anymore though. Still, the name remains)The actual original recipe had cocaine in it and was sold as a medicinal pick me up. Later, as cocaine was made illegal, they still used the coca leaf extract minus the cocaine alkaloid  in CocaCola. Even today, they are the only company that can still import coca leaf and coca leaf extract (under some serious oversight) so they can continue to make  their product. As the war on drugs, and cocaine in particular, really ratcheted up in the early to mid  80's,  Getting the coca leaves became difficult enough that The Coca Cola Company tried to pass off "New Coke" because it was cheaper to produce with less hassle. It was basically Pepsi with more sugar and in a red can. Customers hated it. The Coca Cola Company lost enough money that they decided to introduce Coke Classic which was the same soda they abandoned only a few years before, only in a re labeled can. Not long after, "New Coke" vanished altogether. Then Pepsi released Pepsi Clear. No Idea who thought that up or why.

Props to you for using the actual ingredients to make the flavouring combination rather than just buying a bunch of essential oils. You need to be a bit careful with the bottled essential oils - many of them are sold in very high concentrations, way higher than you could extract from the food ingredients you used, and so are not necessarily safe to ingest (especially since some can also cause nasty side-effects in people with certain medical conditions.) That's what winds me up slightly about the DIY-health-and-beauty approach to aromatherapy that some health food shops and publications tout these days; it paints all these essential oils as nothing more than health-boosting perfumes. The truth is, some of them can be downright dangerous if you don't know the right dosage, the medical history of the person using them and the potential side-effects they can cause.

Colas are typically a soda phosphate style beverage with a hint of citric to round the taste but not so much it kills the natural tang of the phosphate. Using citric acid alone can not replicate this flavor and explains why the color is wrong. Also, a very minor amount of freeze dried coffee and a drop of vanilla extract (the instant mix) can help with both the color and the flavor.

Total CLICKBAIT! You need Kola nuts to at least call this drink a Cola. The recipe you showed is very similar to that of CHINOTTO. It's an Italian drink made with a fruit similar to oranges, but bitter and sour in taste + sparkling water, orange and lemon juice, coffee, sugar cane etc. Chinotto's recipe was used also to create Fanta by Germany during WWII and then by Albania to make Aranxhata (OrangeJuice) during the totalitarian regime. Chinotto's taste actually has some very subtle elements that make you think of Coca Cola, because Colas probably use the Chinotto fruit (Neroli or Bitter Orange from your POV), sugar cane and lime peels.
